LIBRARY 
# Headwind Hesket Grain Land Library for X-Plane 11: October 30, 2020. Add 3 Bedroom brick houses LH and RH.
# FTC and GBI finished trim.  Now move some Grain Storage objects to unused cache to get to fewer than 4800 objects.
# Wichia Metro still needs to be examined for missing Grand Land objects that have been trimmmed.
# Iconic Wichita Metro objects are stand alone in Scenery Wichita Metro.
# I am a retired commercial pilot with more the 50 years of experience. and have been flying in Kansas for
# more than 25 years, much of it in piston twins below 10,000 feet. When the sun is low and you are
# flying closer the ground than the big commercial guys above, much of the first thing you see off in the
# far distance in the sunlight is grain elevators and systems, windfarms, and, especially at night,
# radio, tv, and cell towers.  I am trying to re-create the enjoyment felt from that kind of flying in X-Plane.
# The primary purpose of this library is to populate a series of scenery packages I am creating to
# upload to X-Plane soon in late summer, 2020. The libraries, 'Headwind_Grain_Land_Library' and 'Headwind_Water_Tower_Library (about 8000 object),
# along with several of the typical free libraries available from X-Plane.org are required for
# the 'Headwind' series of scenery packages, including: CDB-Library, ff_library, ff_library,extended_LOD,
# Fruitstand-Aircraft, JB_Library, MisterX-Library, NAPS_library, opensceneryx, R2_Library, RE_Library,
# The_Handy_Objects_Library, and Prefab_Library.  I also like 'Treelines_Farms_North_America_v2' as an option.
# The 'Headwind_Water_Tower_Library' contains dozens of Water Tower and Water Tank designs, each with three
# or fours sizes and several colors patterns.  There are over 900 choices of water towers.
# The 'Headwind_Grain_Land_Library' contains three sub-directories: 'HWH_Farm_Town_and_Cities',
# 'HWH_Grain_Belt_Industry', and 'HWH_Grain_Storage', contain a total of about 4300 objects and 600 texture files.
#  Many texture files are dulplicated in each of the three separate object directories. (There are an average of 200 in each directory.)
#
# Most object in these directories have three or four sizes and each size has two to four colors. 
# With many dozens of each styles and type of object results in many hundreds item to choose from.
# Overkill maybe, but you don't have to use the complete library if you 
# only want a individual item and not use the Grain_Land_Library.
# Simply copy the item into your package along with its texture.png (and texture_LIT.png if desired) files.
# Use 'notepad' or similar text editor to see the required .png file(s if LIT).
# Use can use individual objects in your own scenery package and add it into it's library.txt.
# Go online to X-Plane.org to figure that stuff out.  Feel free to use these objects in your
# non-commercial packages. Of course nobody ever minds a thank you.  Commercial guys contact me at headwindh@cox.net
# 
# Farms_Towns_and_Cities contains items such as: Schools, office buildings, parking garages, stores, sports
# facility objects, barracks and dorms, apartments, parking garages and carports, prison facilities,
# hotels, motels, farm and utility buildings, and more.
#
# Grain_Belt_Industry contains items such as: Several types of commercial buildings and offices, storage tanks,
# transformer stations, large and small smoky factories, serveral types and sizes of radio/tv/cellular towers,
# and much more.
#
# Grain_Storage contains: Many types and sizes of grain storage elevators, silos, and bins, and tanks, 
# both as individual grain storage objects and as small and large grain elevator facilities and ethenol plant
# objects in groups and more.
#
#
# I have modeled much of Wichita proper, including many detailed objects depicting actual downtown, and close
# suburban areas in the near vicinity of Wichita in a package called 'Headwind_Scenery_Metro_Wichita_KS'.
# People familiar with Wichita and it's iconic buildings will like the look from the air.
# Credit for the many of the wonderful detailed models of Wichita, KS is given to contributors of open soure
# .skp files for use in Sketchup uploaded to 3D Warehouse.  I have spent many months embossing and retexturing
# altering and re-sizing these free, open sourse objects to make them useable for X-Plane using one texture file.
# Everyone should goto 3D Warehouse from Sketchup to see the wonderful views of these iconic Wichita objects.
# Many thanks to the 3D Warehouse contributors who have provided the basic structures of objects I have used.
# Credit and many thanks is give to: CS3Desgn; sacrotes; Charles A.; Eurogator; builder 1971; David S.; Ben F.;
# Emily G.; Jonathan; Thomas C.; haishan; lane; and Muaz A.  Apoligies to any I have missed giving thanks for contributing.
# I want to give special thanks to Brad S. and CS3Designs for their beautiful, iconic buildings.  Brad S. has
# done a masterful job of creating a beautiful model of Davis Hall at Friends University in Wichita.
# CS3Design has provided worderful models of most of the Wichita models I have used of the iconic buildings downtown.
# People who fly X-Plane over downtown Wichita will appreciate the realistic view of buidings such as; Wichita Workforce,
# Broadway Plaza and Offices; Cita Hall; Transit Center; Executive Center; Commodore Hotel; Midian Shriners; St. Mary's;
# 11 West; Law Company; Weigand; 250 Douglas (Garvey Center); Intrust building; Parking garages; 315 Riverview;
# State Offices; Riverwalk; Riverview; Federal Building.  Go to the 3DWarehouse and see the many CSDesign buildings. 
#
# Having completed the 'Headwind Grain Land Library' which I will upload soon, I am now finishing Scenery Packages
# 'Headwind Grainland Kansas West 1.0', 'Headwind Grainland Kansas East 1.0', and 'Headwind Grainlad Wichita Metro 1.0'.
# 'Kansas West' covers Kansas land and little way into the surrounding States
# depicted on the U.S. Wichita Sectional Chart.  '...Kansas East' covers land in Kansas and a bit of Missouri,
# Oklahoma, and Arkansas shown on the Kansas City Sectional.  'Wichita Metro' of course covers the city of
# Wichita, Kansas and surrounding suburbs.  Each of the three use the 'Headwind Grain Land Library' and are indepentant.
# Most of the Wichita Metro iconic objects and textures are placed directly in the 'object' directory of the 'Metro'
# package as they are very detailed which results in large size object files.  In order to keep the GL Library file
# size as small as feasable the Wichita iconic files are not included in the Grain Land Library.  It is already big.
# 
# The Eastern edge of the 'Wichita' Sectional Chart lies about 30 mile East of Wichita, KS.
# The 'Wichita Sectional' Scenery Package covers West, North and South a little past the Kansas State lines in each direction.
# The 'Kansas City Sectional' Scenery Package covers all of the remaining parts of Eastern Kansas and nearby surrounding States.
#
# The stand-alone 'Headind Grain Land Windfarms 1.0' package attempts to model EVERY wind turbine currently working and depicted
# on the available satallite photos in Kansas and nearby areas surround the state.  More will be added as photos are added.
# I am using wind turbines from the OpenSceneryX Library to place wonderful animated, lighted windfarms.
# Looking out at hundreds of wind turbines all around and out towards the horizon is a big part of lower altidude flying in Kansas.
#
# Almost all of the objects and all of the texture files in the 'Headwind Grain Land Library' are original creations by Headind H.
# Original Headwind H objects files names are preceded with 'HWH_....' and most texture files with 'HWWT...'.
# Some, but not many, objects are modeled after open-use objects downloaded from X-Plane.org or 3D Warehouse. 
# Object files with names beginning with 'HWXP...' or 'HWSU...' are re-modeled and/or re-textured open use files
# downloaded from X-Plane.org or Sketcups 3DWarehouse and modified to give various appearances, sizes, and textures.
# Almost every one of these orginal downloaded files use many texture files in the same model and had to be re-textured
# to satisfy the Sketcup2XPlane Sketchup add-on (downloaded from X-Plane.org) requirment of only one texture file per object.
# Each of these files was re-modeled to suit the desired look and re-painted using single '.png' files created by me.
# Most of my 'HWWT....png' files are 256x256 two color or 512x512 four color patterns.  A few texture files are
# 1024x1024, 2048x2048, or 4096x4096 color pattern with several colors for more detailed texturing.
# Colors size is usually 256 colors for the 2 and 4 panel .png files, reducing texture file storage and memory
# requirments and speeding up loading times.
#
# Feel free to use and or alter the texture file used, for non-commercial use, any of the 'HWH_...' original objects
# in the 'Headwnd Grain Land Library'.  Please do not upload any altered objects using the same filename(s).
# Credit for the work by me in this package is not required but would be nice.
# If an 'HWXP...' or 'HWSU...' object is modified and uploaded to the publice, please mention that the object
# is based on an open-source Sketchup file downloaded from XPlane.org or Sketchup's 3DWarehouse that has
# been modified by Headwind H.
# Thanks to creators of X-Plane, WED, Overlay Editor, Sketchup 14, Sketchup2Xplane, and Paint Shop Pro.
# And thanks again to contributors in XPlane.org and Sketchup 3D Warehouse of open scenery .skp and .obj files
# useble in X-Plane, Sketchup, and Sketchup2XPlane.
# Object files in this library with a name beginning with 'HWH_...', 'HWWT_...', or 'HW_...' are all original
# creations by me, Marvin Hesket.
# 'HWWT_...png' texture files were created by me and may be used or altered freely.  Please to not distribute
# altered files with same filename.
#
#   Changing a .obj color scheme of a Headwind H object directly without editing a Sketchup .skp file
#   and an attempt to explain '..._LIT' texture files.
#
#  Object names containing texture file named such as; '_2TMt-Sc', '4TAA-Scd', 'T3D or T3DMt-Sc' mean things
#  like: '2 Color Panel Texture File', '4 Color Panel Texture', or '3D Multi-Color'.
#  It is easy to re-color a 2T or 4T object in Sketchup, or directly editing the .obj files 'Texture (filename.png) 
#  and Texture_LIT (filename_LIT.png) by using another texture file with the same size and 2 or 4 color panel pattern.
#  'Embossing' doors, windows, and the like into the walls of buildings, roofs edges, etc., shadows give a good look
#  to simple textured objects, especially for 'fly-over' items such as grain elevators, or industrial buildings.
#  To change the color of an object .obj file directly, rename a copy of the object, copy a texture file with
#  a new file name if one does not already exist.  Use a graphics editor like Photo Shop or Paint Shop (my preference)
#  to change the color or shade of each color segement of the texture file as desired. Either change the file name
#  of the object using the new color scheme as desired in the 'Materials/Edit Texture' window of Sketchup if editing 
#  a .skp file in Sktchup or directly edit the finished .obj file with a text editor and edit the
#  texture (and optional texture.LIT) filename(s) to use the new desired color pattern.
#  An optional LIT texture located in the object's text file refers to a texture which is much darker in shade than
#  the main texture with its filename identical to the main texture file except that the letters '_LIT' are added to the
#  end of the file name.  i.e.:A 'small_red_one_story_house.obj' using a texture file '4TRedwhiteBlueBlack.png'.
#  The object's # 	text file would contain in it's file definition text the line 'texture 4TRedWhiteBlueBlack.png.
#  That texture file would be used to paint the object and appear dark and eventially unseeable as night wears on, 
#  unless a matching '_LIT' texture is defined.  If the object text file contains, immediately following the texture
#  definition, the 'texture LIT' definition (i.e. 'texture LIT 4TRedWhiteBlueBlack_LIT.png' X-Plane will blend the two
#  files from full daylight through falling/rising light at dusk/dawn until the full '_LIT' texture is used during the
#  darkest hours.  A dark image with only the glass portion of windows or skylights or the red portions of lamp lenses,
#  or billboards/sign a little brighter will look like lighted portions of the object a night.
#  Only a small bit of lightness in a '_LIT' texture file will cause a bright look in the rendering.  A '..._LIT file should
#  be very dim. Use a texture editor to reduce the brightness and contrast of the entire (daylight) texture file
#  down to the point where only the brightess portion of the file is barely visible to give a nice, floodlight like glow
#  to an object observed at night.  If desired, for instance to shows lighted windows/skylights/billboards/etc brighten up
#  a little more the texture segements used to render to area of object.
#  Remember, when creating an X-Plane object using Sketchup's add-on 'Sketchup2XPlane' and a newly created object's texture
#  file contains a matching '....LIT' file a 'texture LIT' line will be added to the object's text definition.
#  I desired/necessary to have some objects that use LIT properties and some that don't, use different texture files.
#  As an example, if I want a small green and white 25 foot x 20 foot shack to show glowing windows I might create in
#  Sketchup an object 'Shack_Green-White_25x20.obj' that used a texture file 'RedWhiteLtBlueGreen.png'.  If the diretory that
#  Sketch2XPlane used to create the object contained a matching 'RedWhiteLtBlueGreen_LIT.png', Sketch2XPlane would add a
#  'texture _LIT RedWhiteLlBlueGreen_LIT' line in the object's text file.  The '_LIT' texture would be reduced in brightness
#  to almost dark except for a blue segment.  The light segement would show as lighted during darkness.
#  For an identical shack without lighted windows I would use the same daylight texture file copied to a different filename
#  and omit a matching '_LIT' file in the directory containing the texture.  i.e.: 'Shack_Green-White_daylight.obj' textured
#  in Sketchup using the texture without a matching '_LIT'.  i.e: 'RedWhiteBlueGreen.png' (instead of LTBlue).
#  Another method to use or not 'LIT' properties using the same texture file is too edit manually, using a text editor, an objects
#  text file and add or subtract, after the 'texture .....png' line a 'texture LIT .....LIT.png' line and make sure the appropriate
#  texture file with the '_LIT' phrase in the filename exits in the directory used to texture/paint the object.  
#  I am sure the above discussion of '_LIT' texture is clear as mud. Backup .obj files, experiment. Use new file or restore.
#  Good results of rendering objects at night can be pleasing.
#  Please, don't use me a your source of info on '_LIT' textures other than as an introduction. I just used trial and error.
#  See Sketchup, Sketchup2XPlane, and X-Plane.org tutorials and discussions of '_LIT' textures for proper use of '_LIT' textures. 
#
#  Happy flying! Marvin 'Headwind' Hesket.  (X-Plane.org: Headwind H)
#
